## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (mass-action ODE rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a chemical concentration A, which is the standard form of kinetic rate laws. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are single-species depletion/production kinetics (mass-action orders, relaxation to equilibrium, or time-varying effective rate coefficients).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion when A is in large excess or surface-limited)
- Zero-order production: dA_dt = c0 (constant feed/generation into the system)
- First-order decay (mass-action): dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like, many elementary steps under pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or effective second-order behavior)
- General power-law (n-th order): dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global rate law over limited regimes)
- Affine sourceÔÇôsink (CSTR-like balance): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant input with first-order removal leading to steady state)
- Relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (net rate proportional to deviation from equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / self-accelerating with limitation: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (A catalyzes its own formation but is limited by resource/stoichiometry)
- Saturation-limited consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (effective rate saturates at high A due to capacity/active-site limitation)
- Self-inhibition at high concentration: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 * A + 1) (crowding/product-like inhibition represented using only A)
- Time-varying first-order coefficient (linear ramp): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (changing conditions such as temperature/programmed catalyst activity)
- Time-varying first-order coefficient (exponential drift): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (deactivating catalyst or decaying effective rate with time)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (light-driven or periodically modulated reaction conditions)
- Thresholded consumption (onset after induction): dA_dt = -c0 * Max(A - c1, 0) (reaction only proceeds above a critical concentration)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope Ôćĺ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects Ôćĺ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay Ôćĺ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior Ôćĺ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects Ôćĺ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action signature: if dA_dt is proportional to A (straight line in dA_dt vs A through origin), a first-order step is likely.
- Reaction-order inference: a logÔÇôlog linear trend between |dA_dt| and A suggests dA_dt Ôëł -c0 * A**c1, where c1 is the apparent order.
- Equilibrium approach: sign change of dA_dt around a nonzero A indicates relaxation form dA_dt Ôëł -c0 * (A - Aeq).
- Autocatalysis clue: dA_dt increasing with A at low A but decreasing at high A suggests a product form like A*(Amax - A).
- Capacity limitation: if |dA_dt| grows with A then plateaus, use rational saturation forms in A (rate-limited by sites/transport).
- Inhibition/crowding: if |dA_dt| peaks at intermediate A and drops at high A, consider inhibitory denominators (c1*A + 1) or (A + c1).
- Nonstationary conditions: systematic drift of dA_dt at the same A across time implies k depends on t (multiply A by a function of t).
- Physical constraints: concentrations should remain nonnegative, so rate laws often include structures that avoid driving A below 0 (e.g., Max(A-c1,0) or rates that vanish as AÔćĺ0).

- Contains `sin(log(A+1))` ÔÇö this is a very specific nonlinear function

The `sin(log(A+1))` term is critical. Very few candidates will have anything that can produce this. Let me scan for candidates containing `sin(log(...))` or equivalent.

Looking through all candidates, NONE of them contain `sin(log(...))`. The candidates contain:
- `sin(A*c + c)` (Candidates 1, 37)
- `cos(c*t)` (various)
- `log(...)` without sin (Candidate 6, 31)
- `cos(A*c)` (Candidate 40)
- Various rational, exponential, polynomial terms

Since `sin(log(A+1))` is a fundamentally different basis function from any combination of:
- polynomials in A
- rational functions of A
- `A^c` (power functions)
- `exp(A*c)`
- `sin(A*c + c)` (sin of linear function Ôëá sin of log)
- `cos(c*t)`
- `log(A*c + 1)` (without sin wrapper)
- `t/(A*c + c)` or `1/(A*c + c)`

None of these can reproduce `sin(log(A+1))` exactly. The function `sin(log(A+1))` is oscillatory in A (for large A) in a way that no polynomial, rational, exponential, or simple trigonometric function of A can match.

Let me verify there's no candidate with `sin(log(...))`:
- Scanning all 50 candidates... None contain `sin(log(...))`.

Therefore, by the principle of linear independence of basis functions (Rule 3), no candidate can match the GT, since the essential `sin(log(A+1))` term cannot be reproduced by any of the available basis functions in any candidate.
